## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task models the rate of change of concentration dA/dt in a chemical reaction, where the rate law depends on concentration A and possibly explicitly on time t. Classical chemical kinetics provides various rate law forms from zero-order to complex mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order: dA_dt = c0 * A (rate proportional to concentration)
- Second-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (rate proportional to square of concentration)
- nth-order: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (general power-law rate law)
- Mixed order with offset: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (competing first and second order pathways)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with equilibrium)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme kinetics / saturation kinetics)
- Substrate inhibition: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A + c2 * A**2) (enzyme with substrate inhibition)
- Autocatalytic: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalytic reaction)
- Time-dependent first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (reaction with time-varying rate constant)
- Consecutive reaction: dA_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) + c2 * A (rate from intermediate in consecutive scheme)
- Parallel pathways: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 + c2 * A**c3 (multiple reaction pathways)
- Langmuir-Hinshelwood: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A)**2 (surface-catalyzed reaction kinetics)
- Fractional order with time modulation: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * (c2 + t)**c3 (time-dependent catalytic activity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Simple power-law dependence on concentration → nth-order rate law dA_dt = c*A^n, where n is the reaction order
- Rate that levels off at high concentration → Michaelis-Menten or Langmuir-type rational fraction in A
- Quadratic concentration term with opposite sign to linear term → competing forward/reverse or parallel reactions
- Product of A and (constant - A) → autocatalytic or logistic kinetics where product catalyzes its own formation
- Explicit time dependence multiplying A → time-varying rate constant from external forcing (light, temperature ramp)
- Sum of exponential in t plus linear in A → intermediate species from consecutive reaction mechanism
- Rational function with A in both numerator and denominator → enzyme or surface-catalyzed mechanism
- Negative coefficient on leading A term → consumption/decay of reactant A in the reaction

## Analysis

The GT numerical expression is:
`0.2331857324078805*A**0.333333333333333 - 0.3115334933234426*A**2 - 0.3115334933234426*A*exp(-0.08476196603472734*t)`

This has three terms:
1. `c * A^(1/3)` — a fractional power of A
2. `c * A^2` — a quadratic in A
3. `c * A * exp(c*t)` — an exponential decay times A
